# Deep Audit 2026-07-11 — whole-codebase review report

> **Status: session-artifact — immutable historical snapshot.** This is the
> point-in-time record of the whole-codebase deep audit as run against a fork of
> `9a24d453`, re-verified against `main` on 2026-07-11. It is preserved for the
> narrative and the evidence, NOT as a live tracker. **For the current status of
> every finding (open / fixed / mooted / deferred, owning PR, and required
> validation), see the live ledger: [REVIEW-deep-audit-ledger.md](REVIEW-deep-audit-ledger.md).**
> Findings below carry stable `DA-NNNN` ids that the ledger joins on. Method:
> [DEEP-AUDIT-PLAYBOOK.md](DEEP-AUDIT-PLAYBOOK.md).

## Executive summary

This codebase has **very good bones and an accumulating drift tax**. The architecture discipline is real and held up under a line-by-line adversarial read: the extensibility doctrine (registries + protocol seams + single-writer reconcilers) produced only **5 boundary violations across 1,506 files**, safety ceilings are pinned by guard tests, privilege separation is genuinely engineered, and there are **zero credentials in the tree**. A second contributor could trust the *structure* everywhere.

What they could not yet trust is the *periphery*: **1 fabricated doc section + 5 major-drift docs** (including SECURITY.md misstating the control API's bind surface), **93 confirmed dead-code findings** (including a 764-line module with no caller), **169 mapped duplication clusters** (atomic-write hand-rolled 13×, a JSON escaper 7× across 4 Rust crates), a **29-file monster corridor** carrying most of the complexity, and **42 dead/renamed env flags** in docs. None of this is rot — it is single-maintainer velocity outrunning hygiene, and all of it is now mapped to six executable fix waves.

The completeness critic (below, verbatim) validated reader quality 3/3 on independent spot-reads but caught the audit's own blind spots honestly: two real cross-tile bugs were rationalised past (both independently fixed on main the same day), and the audit ran on a fork that main has already moved under. **Read every finding with the rebase-first rule: verify against current main before fixing.** 8 findings are already mooted by main's deletions; ~7 of main's 14 new commits fixed audit-adjacent bugs.


## Honest grades (static audit; confidence + what runtime alone can prove)

| Attribute | Grade | Confidence | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| Boundaries / extensibility | **A−** | High | 5 violations tree-wide; registries/doctrine held everywhere else. The standout strength. |
| Hardware/audio safety | **B+** (static) | Med-high | 0 dB ceilings pinned by test + verified in generators; 4 findings, none catastrophic. **Unverified:** README's "outputd is the only normal writer to the DAC" invariant has no guard test. Runtime behavior unprovable here. |
| Security | **B** | Med-high | No secrets in tree; WS1 privilege separation real. Fixes needed: 3 unguarded POST routes in /ha/ wizard, predictable OAuth `state` in google_setup, /wifi/ returns raw nmcli stderr (PSK-bearing) to browser. |
| Code cleanliness | **B** | High | Duplication is the main tax (169 clusters); 93 dead-code findings; monster corridor (29 files >2k LOC). |
| Tests | **B** | High* | >1,000 hermetic tests, strong guard culture; 39 untested load-bearing gaps, 1 phantom-flag pin, 1 silent no-op assertion, test_doctor.py monolith. *No test was EXECUTED — "tested" = a reader read the test source. |
| Observability | **B−** | High | log_event convention good but absent from the largest wizard (sound_setup) and /wifi/ mutations; 3 of 9 wake-funnel stages never populated. |
| Availability / resilience | **B−** (static) | **Low (runtime)** | 30 findings (unbounded read_form, env_u32 accepts 0 for sample_rate, lock-released-mid-check race, RPC under cache lock). Architecture (reconcilers/guardians/supervisors/watchdog tiers) is strong on paper; months-of-uptime behavior is out of static reach. |
| Documentation | **C+** | High | The weakest axis — and simultaneously a strength: 2,472 *checkable* claims is exceptional doc culture. But: 1 fabricated section (HANDOFF-volume gain_chain), 5 major-drift docs, 39 minor-drift, 42 doc should-fixes, 3 docs citing a doctor.py deleted weeks ago, SECURITY.md/README/PLAN.md factual errors. |

**Coverage claim, honestly stated:** 100% of files opened on the audited fork, with three asterisks — (1) the fork is not main and main has moved; (2) "opened" ≠ "understood across tile seams" (two proven cross-tile misses); (3) static-only: nothing was executed, no hardware was touched.


## What only hardware/runtime can prove
Audio quality/latency under load; AEC behavior; watchdog/recovery ladders actually recovering; deploy-transaction integrity on a real Pi (the mtime trap class); polkit/authority seams under the non-root model (the #1206 class); voice-eval behavior (paid suite not run); months-of-uptime memory behavior on 1 GB.


## What's genuinely strong (earned, not flattery)
- The extensibility doctrine is practiced, not aspirational — 5 violations in 591k LOC.
- Safety-pin test culture: the 0 dB ceiling guard test exists and covers every static CamillaDSP config.
- The reconciler/single-writer pattern is consistently applied (AEC, DAC, identity, WiFi guardian) and was verified as such.
- Zero real credentials anywhere in 1,653 tracked files; secret files use the group-scoped compartment design.
- Doc culture: docs make **falsifiable claims** with verification footers — which is why drift was findable at all. Most projects' docs cannot even be wrong in a checkable way.

## Coverage ledger

- Phase 1: 1,506/1,506 source files opened across 123 tiles (one gap closed by coordinator read). 18 binary/lockfiles skipped with reason. 129 docs deferred to Phase 2 by design → all 138 docs (incl. root) claim-checked there.
- Findings pipeline: 753 raised → 76 rejected by independent Opus verification (~10%) → 677 kept (2 blocker / 264 should-fix / 411 nit). 4 verifier-added.
- Full per-tile ledger and all 677 findings with evidence: Phase 1 artifact + machine-readable JSON (paths below).


## Unknown-unknowns surfaced (Phase 0 → adjudicated)

- Off-map production packages: `jasper/bluetooth/` (running service, no HANDOFF), `jasper/audio_measurement/`, Python `jasper/fanin/`, `c/jts-ring-ioplug` — all absent from doc-map.toml, whose `validate_map()` checks no code globs (CI-invisible).
- `docs/HANDOFF-volume.md` gain-chain section documents a module/test/state-field that never existed, under a verification footer.
- Orphan tooling: `satellite_validation.py` (692 LOC), `airplay-receiver-timing-proof.py` (803 LOC), `_audit_baseline_events.py`, `aec-probe-usb-delay.sh`; `multiroom-spike/` accidental spike output tracked in git.
- Superseded twin `jasper_aec3/src/aec3_binding_v2.cpp`; two duplicate CLEANUP-moode docs; `capture-page/js/level-events.js` built+tested but never imported by the shipped page.
- The 2026-06-21 bulk-touch commit destroyed all mtime-based staleness signal — future audits must use git-blame per hunk.

## Findings snapshot (frozen; stable ids, untruncated evidence)

_This is the immutable record of what the audit found. Current disposition is in the [ledger](REVIEW-deep-audit-ledger.md); do not drive work from this section directly._

### Blockers — 2

- **[DA-0001]** `blocker` · low-quality · `deploy/assets/rooms/js/main.js` :: makeBondCard().sync() — appendChildren call at :730
  - sync() calls `appendChildren(currentSummary, summarize(g))` to render the bond-card summary, but `appendChildren` is never imported or defined anywhere in this file, and dom.js only exports `h`/`svg` (appendChildren is a private, unexported helper there). Every poll cycle where this speaker is bonded (paired/grouped) throws a ReferenceError inside the `if (bonded)` branch, immediately after `currentSummary.textContent = ""` has already cleared the summary but before it is repopulated.
  - _Evidence:_ grep confirms `appendChildren` occurs exactly once in main.js (line 730); main.js's import list is `getJSON, postJSON` / `jtsConfirm` / `localWebHost` / `h, svg` / `createPairBalanceController` / grouping-view exports — no appendChildren. dom.js: `export function h(...)` and `export function svg(...)` only; its internal `function appendChildren(el, children)` (used by h/svg themselves) has no `export`. The throw is caught by update()'s `try { refs.bondCard.sync(snap); } catch (e) { console.error("rooms: failed to sync bond card", e); }`, so the page doesn't blank, but everything after line 730 in the bonded branch never runs: syncBalance(g) (balance slider never enabled/populated from server state), mains-highpass toggle visibility for sub-equipped pairs, the add-subwoofer advanced panel becoming available, and dissolveBtn/swapBtn's proper enable/visibility logic.
  - _Fix:_ Export appendChildren from dom.js and import it in main.js. NOT the reader's native currentSummary.append(...summarize(g)): summarize()'s unrecognised-role fallback returns a nested array (['Paired', [' — ', ...]]) which .append() stringifies rather than recursing; only appendChildren flattens it.
- **[DA-0002]** `blocker` · dead-code · `jasper/capture_relay/alignment.py` :: assert_alignment_confident
  - The alignment-confidence gate — the module's entire reason for existing ('a silently-wrong measurement unless it fails loud, which is what this module does') — is never invoked by any production capture flow, even though room_sweep, sync_marker, and crossover_sweep all set validity.require_alignment=True and are documented as deployed/landed.
  - _Evidence:_ Repo-wide grep for assert_alignment_confident/cross_correlation_alignment/AlignmentError/require_alignment(read) finds callers only in tests/test_capture_relay_alignment.py and the __init__.py re-export. jasper/capture_relay/session.py:_poll_until_capture (lines 331-359) pulls, decrypts, verifies integrity, and returns CaptureResult directly — no alignment call. jasper/web/correction_setup.py, sync_flow.py, correction_crossover_flow.py, jasper/correction/session.py, and jasper/audio_measurement/deconv.py contain zero align/correlate references (grepped each). docs/phone-mic-relay-plan.md (Last updated 2026-07-07) states 'Status: DEPLOYED... daemon adapters are implemented, deployed', lists §15 acceptance criterion 'A weak/ambiguous cross-correlation alignment fails loud (not a silently-wrong measurement)' without a deferred tag, and its Deferred list only defers 'alignment-threshold tuning' (the 0.40 constant), not the gate itself. jasper/audio_measurement/ramp.py:22 confirms a *different* flow tried and abandoned this same function ('An earlier draft reused capture_relay.alignment.cross_correlation_alignment... structurally near-degenerate on a monotonic ramp') — showing the primitive is known-callable but simply was never wired into the sweep-kind flows that actually declare require_alignment=True.
  - _Fix:_ Either wire assert_alignment_confident(wav, known_stimulus, require=spec.validity.require_alignment) into the per-flow adapters that set require_alignment=True, before handing the WAV to analysis; OR, if the integration is genuinely still staged, stop the docs from claiming coverage — move the alignment gate out of the 'DEPLOYED / verify (integrity+alignment)' §11 text and the §15 met-criteria into the Deferred list. Reader's per-adapter + regression-test scope is correct but secondary to picking one of these two.

### Hardening — security / resilience — 204

- **[DA-0003]** `should-fix` · low-quality · `jasper/route_latency/pairing.py` :: pair_events
  - Ambiguity resolution can silently launder a mic detection already flagged as a rejected 'rival candidate' for one tap into a clean match for a DIFFERENT tap, contaminating the latency evidence that feeds hardware-route p95/p99 certification.
  - _Evidence:_ `mic_ambiguous = mic_claim_counts.get(mic_i, 0) > 1` (line ~166) only checks a static 'nearest-claim' count, not the growing `ambiguous_mic_idx` set built by earlier taps' `ambiguous_mic_idx.update(eligible)`. Empirically confirmed by direct execution: taps=[tap(0ms),tap(10ms)], mics=[mic(5ms),mic(15ms)], window_ms=200 -> mic@15ms appears in BOTH `result.ambiguous_mic` (rival for tap@0) and `result.matched` (paired to tap@10ms, raw_delta_ns=5ms). `route_latency_harness.py` feeds `pairing.matched` straight into `latencies_ms` used for certification. No test in test_route_latency_pairing.py checks matched/ambiguous_mic disjointness (existing tests only assert aggregate counts).
  - _Fix:_ Two-pass: first compute all ambiguous taps and union their eligible mics into a poisoned set; in the match pass, treat any tap whose nearest mic is poisoned as ambiguous/unmatched rather than matched. Add a 3-tap regression asserting matched and ambiguous_mic are disjoint.
- **[DA-0004]** `should-fix` · low-quality · `LICENSE` :: :138 (§6 Trademarks), :165 (§9 Accepting Warranty)
  - The repo's operative Apache-2.0 LICENSE text has been altered from the canonical Apache License 2.0 wording in two clauses, diverging from the project's own reference copy at LICENSES/Apache-2.0.txt.
  - _Evidence:_ Full sequence-diff of both files' clause bodies (1.Definitions through END OF TERMS) shows exactly two omissions in LICENSE: §6 drops 'reasonable and customary use in' before 'describing the origin of the Work' (LICENSE:138-141 vs LICENSES/Apache-2.0.txt), and §9 drops 'choose to offer, and charge a fee for,' before 'acceptance of support' (LICENSE:165 reads 'You may accept support, warranty...' instead of the canonical 'You may choose to offer, and charge a fee for, acceptance of support...'). LICENSES/Apache-2.0.txt matches the well-known upstream Apache-2.0 text; LICENSE does not.
  - _Fix:_ Restore §6 and §9 to the exact canonical wording already present in LICENSES/Apache-2.0.txt (add back 'reasonable and customary use in' and 'choose to offer, and charge a fee for, acceptance of'), keeping LICENSE's filled-in copyright appendix.
- **[DA-0005]** `should-fix` · separation-of-concerns · `capture-page/js/main.js` :: boot():604-616
  - room_sweep's server-driven ui/screen payload is computed by the Pi but never read by the phone; main.js hardcodes all copy for this kind instead of using render.js.
  - _Evidence:_ main.js:604 `if (spec.kind === "room_sweep") { renderIntro(screenEl, ctx); }` bypasses render.js's renderScreen entirely; renderIntro/renderPermission/renderMicChoice/renderCalibration/renderPositionCount (lines 181-380) hardcode every string, never reading ctx.spec.screen/ui. jasper/capture_relay/spec.py:604 build_room_sweep_spec's docstring says the ui is "server-driven ... so copy/choreography changes ride a Pi update with no web deploy," and spec.py:687-692 claims sibling kinds need "zero page-renderer change ... every screen reuses the closed component vocabulary." Neither holds for room_sweep: its position-aware heading_text (e.g. "position 2 of 5") is computed server-side and silently discarded.
  - _Fix:_ Cheapest: rewrite build_room_sweep_spec's docstring to say room_sweep's copy is phone-owned and drop the dead position-aware heading_text branch. Routing through renderScreen is the larger correct fix.
- **[DA-0006]** `should-fix` · secret-file-permissions · `deploy/bin/jasper-wifi-guardian` :: L287,290 (nmcli stderr redirect), L297,314 (cleanup); deploy/systemd/jasper-wifi-guardian.service [Service] block (no PrivateTmp=)
  - The boot-time recovery path's `nmcli device wifi connect "$SSID" password "$PSK"` call redirects stderr -- which the script's own scrub_psk() comment says can echo the PSK back -- to `/tmp/wifi-guardian.stderr.$$` via plain shell redirection (created at the shell's default ~0644 mode, not via `mktemp`+`chmod 0600` the way this same script's stash-write path does elsewhere) in the process-wide, non-isolated `/tmp`, because the unit sets no `PrivateTmp=`.
  - _Evidence:_ Lines 287/290: `"$NMCLI" --wait 30 device wifi connect "$SSID" [password "$PSK"] 2>/tmp/wifi-guardian.stderr.$$`; cleaned up only at L297 (success) or after being read for scrubbing at L311-314 (failure) -- an up-to-30s window, or indefinitely if the oneshot is killed before the `rm -f` (e.g. the exact dirty-shutdown scenario this whole guardian exists to survive, per the script's own header comment about the 2026-05-23 incident). deploy/systemd/jasper-wifi-guardian.service has no `PrivateTmp=`, `ProtectSystem=`, or any other hardening directive, unlike its closest architectural siblings -- deploy/systemd/jasper-accessory-reconcile.service and deploy/systemd/jasper-grouping-reconcile-trailing.service (both root-run Type=oneshot reconcilers) -- and ~20 other JTS units, all of which set `PrivateTmp=true`. Without PrivateTmp, that /tmp file is the process-wide, world-readable /tmp any local user/process on the Pi shares.
  - _Fix:_ Add PrivateTmp=true to the unit and capture stderr via mktemp under umask 077.
- **[DA-0007]** `should-fix` · observability · `deploy/systemd/jasper-usbsink.service` :: :134
  - jasper-doctor's zram-swap health check omits 4 of the 11 daemons that actually carry Slice=jts-audio.slice/jts-mic.slice in this tile, including this file.
  - _Evidence:_ grep '^Slice=jts-audio.slice' deploy/systemd/ returns 10 units (incl. jasper-usbsink, jasper-camilla-crossover, jasper-snapserver, jasper-snapclient) plus 1 on jts-mic.slice; jasper/cli/doctor/memory.py:478-486 `_AUDIO_PATH_UNITS` lists only 7 (fanin/outputd/camilla/aec-bridge/shairport-sync/librespot/bluealsa-aplay). This file's own comment (line ~127) credits slice membership with fixing 'the dominant cause of the bursty USB-drop tail' diagnosed 2026-06-28 -- that exact regression class is now undetectable by check_audio_path_no_swap.
  - _Fix:_ Add jasper-usbsink to _AUDIO_PATH_UNITS (snapserver/snapclient optional; camilla-crossover dormant).
- **[DA-0008]** `should-fix` · observability · `firmware/satellite-amoled/src/main.cpp` :: tryConnectStored
  - Status::CONNECTING is written directly into g_status inside the blocking WiFi-join wait loop, never through setStatus()/displayShowStatus(), so the AMOLED panel never renders the documented 'Connecting' state during the up-to-15s join. Contradicts the file's own changelog ('redraws only on state transitions') and docs/satellites.md's Phase-1.2 description.
  - _Evidence:_ main.cpp:139 `g_status = Status::CONNECTING;` then a bare `while(...) { delay(100); }` (144-147), no display call; dial's identical wait loop calls `renderStatus()` every pass (firmware/dial/src/main.cpp:291). loop()'s `lastDrawn` dedupe (603-608) can't catch it either since tryConnectStored runs entirely inside setup(), before loop() executes once.
  - _Fix:_ Change line 139 `g_status = Status::CONNECTING;` to `setStatus(Status::CONNECTING);` — one render persists on the SH8601 for the whole join. Reject the reader's part-2 (retiring loop()'s lastDrawn dedupe): it's an unnecessary, risky safety-net removal, not part of this fix.
- **[DA-0009]** `should-fix` · resilience · `firmware/satellite-amoled/src/main.cpp` :: tryConnectStored / improvConnect
  - Neither WiFi-connect path calls WiFi.setSleep(false). Dial's identically-shaped pair of functions both call disableWifiSleep() on success — a fix added specifically because modem-sleep caused 22-426ms RTT jitter and HTTP POST timeouts on the dial. The satellite's WiFi/Improv code is documented as mirroring dial's skeleton but silently dropped this fix.
  - _Evidence:_ No 'setSleep' anywhere in firmware/satellite-amoled/src/main.cpp (grep confirms). Dial's firmware/dial/src/main.cpp:273-277 defines disableWifiSleep(), called from lines 295 and 338 inside the same two functions (tryConnectStored, improvConnect) satellite-amoled mirrors without it.
  - _Fix:_ Port disableWifiSleep() (or `WiFi.setSleep(false)`) into satellite's tryConnectStored()/improvConnect() success paths, matching dial.
- **[DA-0010]** `should-fix` · security · `jasper/active_speaker/commission_ramp.py` :: _record_ramp_state:198
  - The ramp-progress state file is written via a hand-rolled atomic write with no `os.chmod`, unlike every other active_speaker state writer.
  - _Evidence:_ `_record_ramp_state` does `tmp.write_text(...); os.replace(tmp, path)` with no chmod. calibration_level.py:61, path_safety.py:182, startup_load.py:121, staging.py:125 and web_measurement.py:221 all call `os.chmod(tmp, 0o640)`; camilla_yaml.py's own `_atomic_write_text` docstring explains why: root-owned and non-root jasper-web both read these files.
  - _Fix:_ Add `os.chmod(tmp, 0o640)` before os.replace in _record_ramp_state (or route through the package atomic_write_text at mode=0o640).
- **[DA-0011]** `should-fix` · observability · `jasper/audio_runtime_plan.py` :: _route_policy_errors:1105
  - The shm_ring-coherent early return discards the transport-coherence errors already computed for this plan, instead of just skipping the two loopback/bridge checks below it.
  - _Evidence:_ Lines 1067-1120: `errors = list(transport_coherence_errors(...))` (1074-1080) can contain real Camilla capture/playback device mismatches (transport_coherence_errors lines 1532-1554 check `capture_device != expected_capture` / `playback_device != expected_playback` independent of bridge coherence). But when `normalized_coupling == COUPLING_SHM_RING and ring_pair_is_coherent(...)` (1102-1104), the function does `return ()` (1105) -- discarding `errors` entirely -- rather than `return tuple(errors)`. `ring_pair_is_coherent` (jasper/fanin_coupling.py:321-339) only compares the coupling+bridge tokens, never device names, so it cannot itself vouch for the device match. No test in tests/test_audio_runtime_plan.py combines a coherent shm_ring env with a mismatched `camilla_devices` fixture. The sibling live-status doctor check (`check_outputd_service` in jasper/cli/doctor/audio.py, calling the same `transport_coherence_errors`) got an analogous ring-coherence fix that preserves errors and has a 'keeps its teeth' regression test (tests/test_doctor.py ~3413); this function's fix is less careful.
  - _Fix:_ Change `return ()` at line 1105 to `return tuple(errors)` so transport device-mismatch errors survive the ring-coherence early return; add a coherent-shm_ring + mismatched-devices regression test.
- **[DA-0012]** `should-fix` · observability · `jasper/cli/aec_bridge.py` :: _aec_loop dtln runtime-crash handler (~2147-2160) vs _BridgeStats.set_leg_engine (484)
  - DTLN engine's mid-run crash disables the engine locally but never re-reports it to _bridge_stats, so /run/jasper/aec_bridge_stats.json's leg_engines.dtln stays stuck at the startup value (loaded: true) forever after a runtime failure.
  - _Evidence:_ set_leg_engine("dtln",...) is called only at lines 1826/1838/1848 (pre-loop setup). The in-loop except block (`dtln_engine = None; dtln_clean = b""`) has no set_leg_engine call. jasper/cli/doctor/aec.py:_assess_dtln_engine_from_stats trusts leg["loaded"] verbatim; its journal fallback _assess_dtln_engine only recognizes "DTLN-aec engine enabled"/"DTLN couldn't load", not the runtime "process() crashed" line. Both doctor paths miss a mid-run crash.
  - _Fix:_ In the in-loop DTLN except-block add _bridge_stats.set_leg_engine('dtln', enabled=True, loaded=False, error=str(e)); teaching the journal parser the runtime-crash line is optional/secondary.
- **[DA-0013]** `should-fix` · hardware-safety · `jasper/cli/xvf_firmware_update.py` :: update
  - update()'s own declared subprocess timeouts (systemctl stop=30s + _run_dfu_flash=120s + _wait_for_expected_profile=30s + final reconcile restart=45s = 225s, not counting the download) exceed the wrapping systemd unit's TimeoutStartSec=180s (deploy/systemd/jasper-xvf-firmware-update.service).
  - _Evidence:_ Read all four timeout constants directly in xvf_firmware_update.py (lines ~213,214,159,228) and TimeoutStartSec=180 in the .service file. systemd's default KillMode=control-group means a TimeoutStartSec expiry SIGKILLs the whole cgroup, including a still-running dfu-util child.
  - _Fix:_ Raise TimeoutStartSec in jasper-xvf-firmware-update.service to comfortably exceed the worst-case step sum (e.g. 300s) and add a comment tying it to the in-script timeouts so they can't drift.
- **[DA-0014]** `should-fix` · separation-of-concerns · `jasper/control/server.py` :: _make_handler / class Handler
  - _make_handler (def at line 1356) nests one Handler(BaseHTTPRequestHandler) class that runs to line 3228 (`return Handler`) — 1873 lines, 52% of the file — owning all 28 route methods (11 GET + 17 POST) for at least 5 largely-independent concerns: volume/transport/source, voice/mic/session/cue, AEC/wake, grouping, and system/diagnostics/debug. Each group already delegates to its own already-extracted backing module (volume_ops.py, aec_endpoints.py, jasper.multiroom.*, system_metrics.py) with essentially disjoint imports.
  - _Evidence:_ Verified 28 `_get_*`/`_post_*` methods via grep (lines 1756-3180) inside one class body. docs/REVIEW-2026-06-12-oss-due-diligence.md:316 explicitly lists “Decompose control/server.py (aec_endpoints/uds/state/volume/dial)” as wanted; that logic-layer split is done (aec_endpoints.py 838 LOC, state_aggregate.py 1413 LOC, volume_ops.py 296 LOC, dial.py 167 LOC) but the HTTP-handler-method layer was never carved out to match.
  - _Fix:_ It is already tracked as Phase-1.1 in the OSS review doc and is not a launch blocker; if acted on, the mixin split (handlers/{volume,voice,aec,grouping,system}.py composed in _make_handler, keeping do_GET/do_POST and route tables in server.py) is the right shape. Otherwise leave it as the tracked debt it already is.
- **[DA-0015]** `should-fix` · resilience · `jasper/correction/autolevel.py` :: AutolevelController.run._graceful_stop
  - _graceful_stop's fade-down loop and its final lock-value volume set both swallow set_main_volume_db failures with a bare except-and-continue and NO logging at all, unlike every other exception path in this file.
  - _Evidence:_ Lines ~177-180: `try: await set_main_volume_db(cur)\nexcept Exception:  # noqa: BLE001\n    break` and lines ~190-194: `try: await set_main_volume_db(lock_value_db)...\nexcept Exception:  # noqa: BLE001\n    pass` -- no logger call in either branch. Contrast with the sibling restore_listening_volume_if_ramped(), which does `logger.exception("autolevel volume restore on measurement end failed...")` on the identical failure class, and with run()'s own outer handler which logs `logger.exception("autolevel failed")`. _graceful_stop is the exit path for LOCKED/CANCELLED/MAXED_OUT/safety-timeout; for CANCELLED/ERROR terminal states, restore_listening_volume_if_ramped never retries (`if al.status not in (LOCKED, MAXED_OUT): return`), so a setter failure there has no other safety net. No test in tests/test_correction_autolevel.py injects a failing set_main_volume_db.
  - _Fix:_ Add a logger.warning on the final lock-value set_main_volume_db failure (the fade-down break is best-effort quieting, so logging it too is optional); a targeted test injecting a failing setter during cancel would lock the behavior.
- **[DA-0016]** `should-fix` · resilience · `jasper/cues/manager.py` :: AudioCueManager.regenerate :186
  - regenerate()'s per-cue loop lets one cue's exhausted-retry synthesis failure abort the whole batch, so sibling not-yet-cached cues are skipped for that pass instead of being attempted independently.
  - _Evidence:_ `for cue in cues: ... write_cue(...)` -- write_cue propagates synthesis exceptions by design (documented in both write_cue's and regenerate's own docstrings). The daemon's startup task (_schedule_cue_regen, jasper/voice/daemon_main.py) calls manager.regenerate() as one unfiltered batch inside a single try/except, so cue #1's failure prevents cues #2-7 from being attempted even though generator.py's own docs note Gemini TTS failures are often text-specific (~60% on some inputs), not categorical outages.
  - _Fix:_ Wrap write_cue/prune_stale in a per-cue try/except inside the for-loop, logging and continuing so one bad cue doesn't block its siblings.
- **[DA-0017]** `should-fix` · resilience · `jasper/measurement/volume_guard.py` :: _set_snapcast_snapshot
  - The snapcast client restore loop used in normalized_pair_volumes()'s finally block aborts on the first client RPC failure, leaving any later clients stuck at the calibration volume (100%, unmuted) instead of restored to household levels.
  - _Evidence:_ _set_snapcast_snapshot() (lines 184-217) is `for client in clients: ...; if not ok: raise VolumeGuardError(...)` with no per-client isolation; called unconditionally from finally (line 273) to restore. test_normalized_pair_volumes_restores_after_partial_snapcast_failure only covers a normalize-phase failure where the subsequent restore itself succeeds for all clients — no test exercises a restore-phase failure.
  - _Fix:_ Add a best_effort flag to _set_snapcast_snapshot so the restore call try/excepts each client and collects errors instead of raising on the first, plus a test failing a middle client during restore.
- **[DA-0018]** `should-fix` · resilience · `jasper/multiroom/reconcile.py` :: _ensure_unit_active:1226-1274
  - _ensure_unit_active reimplements the 'systemctl reset-failed' subprocess call inline instead of calling the adjacent _reset_failed_unit() helper, and its except clause is narrower than that helper's.
  - _Evidence:_ Lines 1238-1241 duplicate _reset_failed_unit's subprocess.run body (1166-1169) but without its `except (FileNotFoundError, OSError)` (1170) or its warning log_event. _ensure_unit_active's own try only catches FileNotFoundError/CalledProcessError, so a bare OSError (e.g. fork failure under memory pressure) propagates uncaught.
  - _Fix:_ Replace the inline reset-failed with a call to _reset_failed_unit(unit), and widen _ensure_unit_active's except on the start call to (FileNotFoundError, OSError).
- **[DA-0019]** `should-fix` · resilience · `jasper/multiroom/snapcast_rpc.py` :: _ProbeCache.read
  - The TTL cache's blocking snapserver RPC call runs INSIDE the cache lock, so concurrent /state and /rooms.json pollers serialize behind the in-flight probe instead of getting an immediate cached value.
  - _Evidence:_ `with self._lock:` wraps `self._value = read_stream_clients(url=url, transport=transport)` (the network call itself). Sibling module jasper/multiroom/airplay_latency.py's cached_notified_frames() deliberately reads OUTSIDE its lock, with an explicit comment: 'the reader runs OUTSIDE the lock so a slow journalctl cannot serialize concurrent requests.' _ProbeCache's own docstring states the goal is to prevent 'a snapserver failure [from] turning into a sluggish dashboard' — which this implementation only partly achieves (no second RPC call is made, but concurrent callers still block for up to _RPC_TIMEOUT_SEC=1.0s each).
  - _Fix:_ Mirror cached_notified_frames: under the lock decide staleness and return the current cached copy; if stale, release the lock, probe unlocked, then re-acquire briefly to store.
- **[DA-0020]** `should-fix` · resilience · `jasper/peering/daemon.py` :: ARBITRATE_RPC_TIMEOUT_SEC
  - The RPC's fail-open timeout is a fixed 0.5s — exactly equal to arb_window_ms's own max clamp (500ms), not "modestly higher" as the comment claims. At that configuration there is no guaranteed margin between the real state-machine decision and the timeout's fail-open WIN, risking a race where a stale fail-open WIN and the real StartSession/StandDown disagree.
  - _Evidence:_ "ARBITRATE_RPC_TIMEOUT_SEC = 0.5" (daemon.py:87) vs config.py:309-313 `_parse_int(src.get("JASPER_PEER_ARB_WINDOW_MS"...), lo=50, hi=500)`. No test exercises arb_window_ms=500 together with the real (non-monkeypatched) RPC timeout — tests/test_peering_daemon.py monkeypatches the timeout itself for its edge-case tests.
  - _Fix:_ Derive the RPC timeout as arb_window_sec + a fixed margin (e.g. +150ms) instead of a hardcoded 0.5s.
- **[DA-0021]** `should-fix` · correctness · `jasper/peering/state.py` :: _on_peer_claim
  - Receiving ANY foreign CLAIM — even for a totally unrelated epoch from a peer we've never interacted with — unconditionally forces state=SUPPRESSED, silently clobbering our own in-progress WINNER/ACTIVE session. Since the multicast group is shared by the whole household regardless of which wake it belongs to, an unrelated wake+claim elsewhere in the house (e.g. a second person in another room) tears down our own live conversation's bookkeeping.
  - _Evidence:_ Lines 393-402 set state=SUPPRESSED unconditionally; the WINNER check (line373) and CANDIDATE check (line387) both require a state match, so ACTIVE falls through untouched. TIMER_HEARTBEAT_SEND isn't cancelled, so the next tick hits `_send_heartbeat_and_reschedule`'s `state is not ACTIVE` guard (line549) and silently stops rescheduling; `_on_voice_ended`'s same guard (line456) then also drops BroadcastEnd for the real session.
  - _Fix:_ Add an ACTIVE guard: ignore an unrelated foreign CLAIM while ACTIVE (mirroring _on_peer_wake's 'out of band' case 3), so a live session isn't silently clobbered.
- **[DA-0022]** `should-fix` · correctness · `jasper/usbsink/output_mode_reconcile.py` :: set_output_mode · _(mooted on main)_
  - set_output_mode('fifo', ...) writes JASPER_USBSINK_OUTPUT_MODE and restarts jasper-usbsink.service, but that unit now execs the Rust jasper-usbsink-audio binary, which never reads that env var — arming the lean lane would silently no-op the FIFO writer while CamillaDSP switches to reading a pipe nobody feeds.
  - _Evidence:_ rust/jasper-usbsink-audio/src/*.rs has zero hits for JASPER_USBSINK_OUTPUT_MODE/fifo (grepped). deploy/systemd/jasper-usbsink.service ExecStart is that Rust binary. jasper/mux.py:756-759 _enter_lean already calls omr.set_output_mode('fifo',...) when JASPER_LEAN_LANE fires. ArmResult.ok only confirms env-write+restart succeeded, not that the daemon understood the mode. This module's own docstring names this exact scenario the 'inviolable' no-silent-failure invariant.
  - _Fix:_ Delete the now-superseded lean-lane fifo wiring (mux._enter_lean/_leave fifo arm + output_mode_reconcile's fifo path) per HANDOFF's 'converge to one path / delete the lean lane' note now that Rust owns the data plane; alternatively make set_output_mode verify the restarted daemon actually applied the mode before returning ok=True.

  - Four INFO-level logs dump raw Python id() values, in two near-duplicate pairs, left over from a specific historical bug hunt — journal noise with no ongoing diagnostic value.

- **[DA-0024]** `should-fix` · resilience · `jasper/voice/openai_session.py` :: OpenAIRealtimeConnection._dispatch_function_call
  - The function_call_output wire-send is not wrapped in try/except, unlike every sibling send in OpenAIRealtimeTurn; a failure here (e.g. a tool returning a non-JSON-serializable payload) escalates to _receive_loop's broad except and forces a full session reconnect instead of a contained per-tool error.

Compare send_audio (302-310), end_input (392-401), submit_recorded_audio (358-376), which all wrap their sends and set _turn_lost=True on failure. dispatch_tool() in jasper/tools/__init__.py does not itself validate that a tool's dict payload is JSON-serializable.
  - _Fix:_ Wrap the json.dumps+_send_event in try/except; log and continue (or send a synthetic {"error":...} output) instead of propagating to a full reconnect.
- **[DA-0025]** `should-fix` · resilience · `jasper/wake_corpus/bridge_session.py` :: voice_daemon_active:2107
  - voice_daemon_active() calls `systemctl is-active` with no timeout and no exception handling, unlike its near-identical sibling aec_bridge_active() ten lines below.

  - 3 of 9 documented wake-event funnel stages (response_started, tool_called, tool_completed) and the tool_name column are never populated by any production code path, though the schema, store API, and a recently-"verified" HANDOFF doc all present the full funnel as shipped.

- **[DA-0027]** `should-fix` · resilience · `jasper/web/_common.py` :: read_form
  - read_form(), the one centralized body parser shared by roughly 13 wizard POST handlers package-wide, has no upper bound on Content-Length and does not guard the int() parse against a non-numeric header — both gaps every sibling JSON-body reader in the package at least partially covers.
  - _Evidence:_ _common.py:640-648: `length = int(handler.headers.get('Content-Length') or '0'); raw = handler.rfile.read(length)...` has no max check and no try/except around the int() parse. `grep -rn read_form tests/` shows every test mocks it out — the function's own parsing behavior, including this edge case, is never directly exercised.
  - _Fix:_ Bound length to a shared max constant and try/except the int() parse, returning {} on malformed input; nginx 1m cap is only a production mitigation, not a code guard.

- **[DA-0030]** `should-fix` · security · `jasper/web/home_assistant_setup.py` :: do_POST (/discover, /ready, /verify branches)
  - The POST routes /discover (line 1067), /ready (1072), and /verify (1083) never call guard_read_request() or guard_mutating_request() — every other route in this file, and every route in every other file in this tile, calls one of the two.
  - _Evidence:_ do_POST dispatches straight into discover_sync()/ready_sync()/verify_sync() with no guard call; only /credentials-for-copy (1095), /save, /disconnect call guard_mutating_request. nginx uses `server_name _` + `default_server` (deploy/nginx-jasper.conf:35-37), so there is no upstream Host check either — these Python guards are the only defense against DNS-rebinding. guard_mutating_host's own docstring names 'HA tokens' as exactly what this class of guard protects. /verify leaks the configured HA URL, instance name, version, and conversation-agent list to any origin able to DNS-rebind to the speaker's LAN address. - **[DA-0031]** `should-fix` · separation-of-concerns · `jasper/web/rooms_setup.py` :: _self_addresses / _lan_target / _post_grouping_to_member / _resolve_bond_peer / _discover_speakers_cached / _request_control_token (lines ~173-980, ~1386-1471)
  - The cross-speaker 'peer control-plane' primitives (SSRF-guarded LAN target resolution, member POST/GET to jasper-control, bounded-concurrency fan-out, roster-first bond-peer resolution, control-token relay, cached mDNS discovery) are private (underscore) functions of this page module, but three OTHER independently-deployed web page modules import them directly across the module boundary.

  - _Fix:_ Smallest honest fix: de-underscore the ~6 shared peer-control primitives in rooms_setup (make them public package-shared names) so the cross-module dependency stops masquerading as private; extracting to jasper/multiroom/peer_client.py is the fuller option but not required.
- **[DA-0032]** `should-fix` · observability · `jasper/web/sound_setup.py` :: :177
  - The file never imports or uses `jasper.log_event.log_event`, the codebase's canonical structured-event emitter (added 2026-06-15, PR #699). It instead hand-rolls ~102 `logger.info/warning/exception("event=sound.xxx k=%s ...", ...)` calls throughout — exactly the unescaped, drift-prone pattern `log_event`'s own module docstring says it exists to replace.
  - _Evidence:_ `grep -c` found 102 raw logger.* calls and zero `log_event` references in this file. `grep -rl log_event jasper/web/*.py` shows ~20 sibling wizard modules (correction_setup, speaker_setup, wake_setup, spotify_setup, voice_setup, etc.) have already migrated. log_event.py's docstring: "each call site re-implements the rendering, and none of them escape field values ... silently corrupts the key=val parse".
  - _Fix:_ Migrate to log_event(logger, "sound.xxx", key=value); prioritize the /profiles/* and reason=%s lines that interpolate client-supplied values.
- **[DA-0033]** `should-fix` · hardware-safety · `jasper/web/sound_setup.py` :: Handler.do_POST
  - 13 active-speaker POST routes call their payload builders with no local try/except, unlike ~15 sibling routes in the same handler that wrap the identical call shape in `except OSError` (or broader) and return a clean `{"error": ...}` 502. This includes `/active-speaker/commission-ramp-abort` (the documented "hard Stop: re-mute + reset the ramp" path, line 5037), `/active-speaker/commission-rollback` (5010), `/active-speaker/rollback-startup-config` (4992), `/active-speaker/commission-load` (5001) and `/active-speaker/commission-ramp-step` (5019).
  - _Evidence:_ Traced do_POST's dispatch: the only enclosing try/except is `except (UnicodeDecodeError, json.JSONDecodeError, ValueError)` at line 5193. An OSError/RuntimeError from e.g. `abort_ramp`/`rollback_driver_commissioning_config` is not caught there, so it propagates out of do_POST; stdlib ThreadingHTTPServer's default `handle_error` then prints a bare traceback to stderr (bypassing this codebase's `logger`/`event=` convention) and drops the connection with no JSON body.
  - _Fix:_ Wrap these routes' calls in `except (OSError, RuntimeError) as e: self._send_json({"error": str(e)}, status=502)` to match siblings; the audio path already fails closed, so this only fixes the ugly 500 on secondary I/O faults.
- **[DA-0034]** `should-fix` · resilience · `jasper/web/sync_flow.py` :: handle_play
  - handle_play (line 203) checks `_state["playback"] is not None` under `_lock`, releases the lock, then spawns the aplay subprocess, then re-acquires the lock to set `_state["playback"]`. Two concurrent /sync/play calls can both pass the check and both spawn overlapping marker-playback processes.
  - _Evidence:_ Sibling balance_flow.handle_ramp (jasper/web/balance_flow.py:578-653) does the same spawn-outside-the-lock dance but explicitly re-validates phase/session_token/ramp-not-None in a second `with _lock` block after the spawn and terminates the just-spawned proc on a losing race (lines 615-632). sync_flow.handle_play has no equivalent re-validation or token, so a race silently produces two overlapping markers feeding into the acoustic delay measurement analyzed by handle_analyze.
  - _Fix:_ After run_async, re-acquire _lock, re-check phase=='measuring' and playback is None, terminate the just-spawned proc if state changed.
- **[DA-0035]** `should-fix` · secret-exposure · `jasper/web/transit_setup.py` :: _apply_save() L375; _bus_card_html() L751-753; _citibike_card_html() L971-973
  - Three broad `except Exception as e` handlers in the /transit/ wizard interpolate the raw exception via `%r` / an f-string instead of routing it through `jasper.transit.base.scrub_secrets()`, which this exact feature area defines and correctly uses in its sibling files. L751-753 is the worst instance: it both logs `%r` of the raw exception AND assigns `error = f"unexpected error: {e}"`, which is then `html.escape()`-d straight into the wizard's visible error banner -- not just a log line.
  - _Evidence:_ jasper/transit/providers/nyc_bus.py's own find_stops_near/validate_credentials wrap httpx errors as `TransitError(f"...: {scrub_secrets(e)}")`, and the runtime SIRI client jasper/bus.py (`_fetch_for_stop`) scrubs on BOTH its `httpx.HTTPError` branch and its broad `except Exception` branch: `err=scrub_secrets(repr(e))`, with the comment "httpx.HTTPError repr includes the full URL with ?key=... ; scrub before logging so the key never lands in journalctl." jasper/web/transit_setup.py's `_apply_save`/`_bus_card_html`/`_citibike_card_html` never adopted that same discipline for their outer `except Exception` catch-alls: `logger.warning("bus credential probe raised: %r", e)` (L375), `logger.warning("bus stops fetch raised: %r", e); error = f"unexpected error: {e}"` (L752-753), and the same pair for citibike (L972-973, though citibike is keyless so carries no live secret -- it shows the pattern was copy-pasted rather than a one-off). Any exception type not already normalized to TransitError by the provider (an unanticipated httpx/library exception) would leak the live JASPER_MTA_BUSTIME_KEY both to the journal and to the HTTP response body served on the household LAN.
  - _Fix:_ Wrap e with transit.base.scrub_secrets() (or type(e).__name__) at all three sites.
- **[DA-0036]** `should-fix` · resilience · `jasper/web/weather_setup.py` :: _seed_transit_from_weather_if_missing
  - weather.env is written by two independent wizard threads inside the same jasper-web process (weather_setup.py's own save/clear, and transit_setup.py's mirror-image _seed_weather_from_transit_if_missing) via plain read-then-write write_env_file, not the flock-protected locked_update_env_file the codebase already uses for the identical cross-writer shape.

Both wizards run as threads of one jasper-web process per jasper/web/__main__.py's WizardSpec table. jasper/atomic_io.py's locked_update_env_file docstring names exactly this race ('two writers that both read the old file... and then publish whole-file replacements'), and jasper/web/wake_setup.py + jasper/control/aec_endpoints.py already use it for the analogous wake_model.env two-writer case. No test exercises concurrent weather+transit saves.
  - _Fix:_ Route weather_setup save/clear and the transit seed writers to locked_update_env_file (as wake_setup/aec_endpoints do) so concurrent weather+transit saves can't clobber a location write.
- **[DA-0037]** `should-fix` · secret-exposure · `jasper/web/wifi_setup.py` :: _readable_nmcli_error() L794-800, used by connect_new() L1019/L1040, surfaced via do_POST L1344-1356
  - The /wifi/ wizard's connect-failure path returns nmcli's raw, unscrubbed stdout/stderr straight to the browser as the JSON error message, even though the just-submitted household WiFi PSK was passed to that same nmcli invocation on argv (`nmcli ... device wifi connect SSID password <PSK>`, built in _connect_wifi_command L777-789 and run via _run_nmcli_secret L1018).
  - _Evidence:_ _readable_nmcli_error(proc) does `err = (proc.stderr or proc.stdout or "").strip()` with only cosmetic `Error:` / `Connection activation failed:` prefix-trimming -- no PSK scrubbing. connect_new() sets `err = _readable_nmcli_error(proc)` on failure and returns it as the human-readable message; do_POST ships it verbatim: `self._send_json({"ok": ok, "message": msg}, status=200 if ok else 502)`. This codebase already knows nmcli can echo the PSK back in error text -- deploy/bin/jasper-wifi-guardian carries a dedicated `scrub_psk()` whose comment says it "defends against nmcli quoting the PSK as 'PSK' in echo-back errors" -- but that scrubber was never applied on the Python wizard side. tests/test_web_wifi_setup.py's only connect-failure test (test_connect_new_rolls_back_on_failure) mocks stderr as a generic "Error: Connection activation failed." string, so it doesn't exercise (or guard against) the PSK-echo case at all.

- **[DA-0038]** `should-fix` · observability · `jasper/web/wifi_setup.py` :: do_POST
  - The primary mutating actions (/connect, /forget, /radio) never call log_event; only the best-effort guardian-stash and profile-hardening side effects get structured events.

- **[DA-0039]** `should-fix` · resilience · `jasper/xvf/xvf_host.py` :: DEFAULT_TIMEOUT_MS
  - The 100-second default USB control-transfer timeout used by ReSpeaker.read/write can outlast systemd's default unit-start timeout for the boot-blocking jasper-aec-init.service, which sets no TimeoutStartSec override.
  - _Evidence:_ DEFAULT_TIMEOUT_MS = 100_000 (line 39) is used unconditionally as ReSpeaker.TIMEOUT (line 245) on every ctrl_transfer call (lines 255-262, 271-278). deploy/systemd/jasper-aec-init.service is Type=oneshot, gates Before=jasper-aec-bridge.service jasper-camilla.service, and has no TimeoutStartSec=, so systemd's ~90s default would kill the unit before a single wedged transfer's own 100s timeout fires.
  - _Fix:_ Add TimeoutStartSec (e.g. 120s) to jasper-aec-init.service, or lower DEFAULT_TIMEOUT_MS well under the systemd default.
- **[DA-0040]** `should-fix` · resilience · `rust/jasper-fanin/src/config.rs` :: env_u32 (:963) / Config::from_env sample_rate,period_frames (:471-472)
  - env_u32 (used for sample_rate and period_frames, among ~15 other knobs) parses ANY u32 including 0 — there is no `parsed == 0` rejection anywhere in Config::from_env for these two load-bearing fields. JASPER_FANIN_PERIOD_FRAMES=0 or JASPER_FANIN_SAMPLE_RATE=0 therefore construct a valid Config. Downstream, Mixer::step (mixer.rs:1498, the DEFAULT per-lane hot path, unconditional on coupling mode) calls drain_input_excess(input, period_frames) (mixer.rs:1572) -> catchup_drain_periods (mixer.rs:2247), which does raw `(avail - target) / period_frames` (mixer.rs:2255) with only a `debug_assert!(period_frames > 0)` guard that is compiled OUT in release (Cargo.toml's [profile.release] sets no debug-assertions). The very first period with avail>0 (near-instant) divides by zero and panics. Cargo.toml sets `panic = "abort"`; deploy/systemd/jasper-fanin.service uses `Restart=on-failure`/`RestartSec=5`, so this is an infinite crash-restart loop that kills ALL audio, including any audible-cue path for the failure itself — directly the house-bar-prohibited pattern.
  - _Evidence:_ config.rs:963-971 env_u32 body has no `== 0` check; mixer.rs:2247-2256 catchup_drain_periods debug_assert!+raw divide; mixer.rs:1228 `(config.period_frames as u64) * 1_000_000_000 / (config.sample_rate as u64)` (ShmRing path) is a second unguarded divide-by-sample_rate site.
  - _Fix:_ Add `if parsed == 0 { anyhow::bail!("{} must be > 0", name); }` to fanin's env_u32 (mirroring rust/jasper-outputd/src/config.rs:778), which fixes both sample_rate and period_frames at once.
- **[DA-0041]** `should-fix` · resilience · `rust/jasper-fanin/src/host_compliance.rs` :: RevalidationTracker::step
  - On the first period of a fresh lock (rising edge) that follows ANY prior lock whose EarlyUnlock strike armed-then-properly-expired, step() spuriously re-ARMs a phantom pending strike using the PRIOR lock's stale periods_since_lock/unlock_baseline_at_lock — contradicting the documented invariant 'the next lock is armed clean' (L437) and 'pending_strike_armed ... [n]ever survives a session' (L499). This isn't the already-accepted <=5s-restart residual (L438-444/1291-1307 of docs/HANDOFF-usb-low-latency.md) since it fires no matter how long ago the prior lock ended.
  - _Evidence:_ L617-619 compute within_early_window/unlock_advanced, and L635-638 ARM, all reading self.periods_since_lock/self.unlock_baseline_at_lock; the rising-edge reset of those SAME fields (L672-677, gated on the identical `rising_edge` computed at L597) runs AFTER, in the same call. unlock_for_underfill always sets locked=false in the period it bumps unlock_count (lane_resampler.rs:727-730), so a genuine arm never coincides with locked=true -- meaning within_early_window's `locked ||` disjunct (L618) is dead for legitimate arms and only ever fires on this stale rising-edge read. Traced concretely: Lock A arms within its window then expires (no relock); Lock B's very next rising edge re-arms a strike anchored to Lock A's leftover baseline/window, which can then let a genuinely-churning Lock B's own later underfill+relock cycle fail to CONFIRM (the inherited clock expires before the real relock arrives) -- an under-detection of real host non-compliance. Existing test tracker_relock_just_outside_horizon_does_not_revoke (L1596-1626) only asserts revoke==None on that relock and never checks pending_strike_armed() afterward, so it doesn't catch the phantom re-arm.
  - _Fix:_ Drop the `locked ||` disjunct at L618 so the arming predicate is `falling_edge && periods_since_lock <= early_window_periods`; this preserves every legitimate falling-edge arm (unlock_advanced is always false during locked periods) and kills the phantom re-arm. Add a regression asserting !pending_strike_armed() on the lock after an expired strike.
- **[DA-0042]** `should-fix` · resilience · `scripts/_extract_wake_corpus.py` :: main():528-537
  - Under --force, main() runs shutil.rmtree(output_dir) with zero path-safety check, unlike the 3 other 'wipe-and-regenerate corpus tooling' scripts in this exact tile.
  - _Evidence:_ Lines 528-537: `if output_dir.exists() and any(output_dir.iterdir()): ... shutil.rmtree(output_dir)` — no blocklist. Compare _build_wake_feature_bank.py, _build_wake_negative_feature_bank.py, and _export_wake_corpus_bundle.py, which all call a `_safe_to_remove_output()` guard blocking '/', Path.home(), Path.cwd(), and the source dir itself before rmtree, each with its own passing unit test (tests/test_build_wake_feature_bank.py:249-253, tests/test_export_wake_corpus_bundle.py:300-303). tests/test_extract_wake_corpus.py has no equivalent assertion.
  - _Fix:_ Before the rmtree, refuse when output_dir.resolve() is in {Path('/'), Path.home(), Path.cwd(), corpus_dir.resolve()}. Note: the sibling's extra 'path under corpus_dir' block would break the existing test (output nested under corpus_dir at test line 349), so port only the exact-match blocklist, not the parents check.
- **[DA-0043]** `should-fix` · low-quality · `scripts/doc-freshness.sh` :: :28-37, epoch_days_ago
  - `-h`/`--help` is broken when passed as the first/only argument: `days=${1:-90}` unconditionally consumes it before the arg-parsing loop ever inspects it for -h/--help, so the script crashes on a raw shell-tool error instead of printing help.
  - _Evidence:_ Directly ran `bash scripts/doc-freshness.sh -h` and `--help` in this checkout: both produce `date: illegal option -- d` (never reach the print-help case arm); `bash scripts/doc-freshness.sh 90 -h` (days given first) correctly prints help, proving the root cause is argument-order, not (only) OS-specific date behavior. tests/test_script_help_excludes_spdx.py already carries a carve-out (expected=None) for this script attributing it solely to 'a GNU date path that errors on BSD/macOS'.
  - _Fix:_ Pre-scan "$@" for -h/--help (or use getopts) before the `days=${1:-90}` assignment so the flag works in any position.
- **[DA-0044]** `should-fix` · low-quality · `scripts/multiroom-spike.sh` :: usage() :528-532
  - Identical bug to s0-sync-bench.sh: `usage()`'s `sed -n '2,/^# ===/p'` stops at the title banner's own closing `# ===` line, so `--help`/no-action output is 3 lines instead of the ~100-line USAGE/SAFETY block (WHAT IT BUILDS, THE SWEEP, safety posture, all flag examples).
  - _Evidence:_ Ran `bash scripts/multiroom-spike.sh --help` directly: 3-line output only. The test file's own docstring says this script was the ORIGINAL 2026-06 SPDX-leak incident this guard test was written to prevent (`tests/test_script_help_excludes_spdx.py` module docstring: "CI caught it for multiroom-spike.sh") — the fix traded a leak bug for a truncation bug, and the test's single-substring assertion doesn't catch the new one.
  - _Fix:_ Same as F0 — anchor the end pattern on the real header-closing marker and tighten the test token for this script.
- **[DA-0045]** `should-fix` · low-quality · `scripts/s0-sync-bench.sh` :: :660,:674
  - `-h|--help` and the no-action fallback both self-extract usage text via `sed '2,6d' "$0" | sed -n '2,/^# ===/p' | sed 's/^# \{0,1\}//'`, but the sed range terminates at the header banner's own closing `# ===` line instead of the real end-of-header marker ~80 lines later, so almost the entire usage block — including the HEARING-SAFETY warning and all `--up`/`--smoke`/`--soak`/`--collect`/`--teardown`/host-config docs — is silently dropped.
  - _Evidence:_ Ran `bash scripts/s0-sync-bench.sh --help` directly: output is exactly the 3-line title banner, nothing else. The dedicated regression test `tests/test_script_help_excludes_spdx.py::test_usage_excludes_spdx_header[s0-sync-bench.sh]` still PASSES (`.venv/bin/python -m pytest tests/test_script_help_excludes_spdx.py -v` -> 5 passed) because it only asserts the substring "s0-sync-bench.sh" is present, which survives inside the truncated title line.
  - _Fix:_ Terminate extraction on the header's true closing `# ===` (the one just before `set -euo pipefail`), not the title-box edge — e.g. skip the first two `# ===` lines or use a fixed line count; and assert a deep token (HEARING-SAFETY/--teardown) in the test.
- **[DA-0046]** `should-fix` · low-quality · `scripts/s0-sync-measure.py` :: run_soak:304
  - Unhandled TypeError crash in the CLOCK-LOCK report line whenever a host's soak log has rate_adjust telemetry but zero positive buffer_level readings.
  - _Evidence:_ buf_min/buf_max/buf_mean default to None when buf_levels is empty (parse_soak_log only appends bl if bl>0). The `ok` computation guards None via `(b['buf_min'] or 0) > 0`, but the print two lines later does `f"buffer={b['buf_min']:.0f}-{b['buf_max']:.0f}"` unguarded. Reproduced directly: `TypeError: unsupported format string passed to NoneType.__format__` when has=True (rate_n>0) and buf_min=None — exactly the degenerate 'buffer drained' case this tool exists to catch.
  - _Fix:_ Default buf_min/buf_max to 0 in parse_soak_log's return dict (keeps the `(b['buf_min'] or 0)>0` ok-check correct and fixes the :.0f format).

### Dead code — 29

- **[DA-0047]** `should-fix` · dead-code · `capture-page/js/level-events.js` :: LevelStreamer
  - LevelStreamer/blockLevel are fully built and unit-tested but unreachable from the shipped page - main.js never imports level-events.js.
  - _Evidence:_ grep across capture-page/ and index.html shows level-events.js is imported nowhere except tests/js/capture_level_events_test.mjs. jasper/capture_relay/spec.py:887 build_level_ramp_spec's docstring says the phone "streams batched, client-timestamped mic-level samples" for kind="level_ramp", and docs/HANDOFF-correction.md:26 states "the phone streams batched level samples from capture-page/js/level-events.js" as current fact. main.js's boot() only special-cases kind==="room_sweep"; a level_ramp spec falls through to the generic path whose onStart() records/uploads a WAV rather than streaming level batches. docs/HANDOFF-correction-revision-plan.md:489 confirms "no shipped surface makes that offer yet" (P3b/P7 pending), so this is dormant, not live-broken - but the HANDOFF-correction.md phrasing overstates completion.
  - _Fix:_ Soften HANDOFF-correction.md's P2 bullet to state the phone-side level-streaming loop is built but not yet wired into the page (P3b/P7).
- **[DA-0048]** `should-fix` · dead-code · `deploy/assets/sound-profile/js/main.js` :: fmtDbfs :193, toneSummary :1600, outputStartupLoaded :1659, quietTestStartupReady :1664, quietTestStagedReady :1671, fetchActiveSpeakerStartupLoad :5589, driverResearchDraftSaved :1483, driverMeasurementCounts :2822, driverCheckRolesForGroup :2814
  - 9 locally-declared functions have zero call sites anywhere in the file or repo (verified: each name's only whole-word occurrence is its own declaration line). Their backing state fields activeSpeaker.startupLoad and activeSpeaker.stagedConfig are likewise only ever set to null (init lines 99-100; reset at 4360/5032/5091-5092) and never populated with a real value anywhere, so the one live reader (the setup-disclosure open-condition OR-chain at lines 712-716) has a permanently-false disjunct.

- **[DA-0049]** `should-fix` · dead-code · `deploy/install.sh` :: camilla_config_has_safe_volume_limit
  - An awk-based CamillaDSP volume_limit safety-ceiling check (0 dB or below) is defined at lines 1048-1070 but is never called from any production code path in install.sh, any deploy/lib/install/*.sh, any deploy/bin/* script, or Python.
  - _Evidence:_ grep across the whole repo for camilla_config_has_safe_volume_limit shows exactly two hits: its own definition and tests/test_install_helpers.py, which sources install.sh only to unit-test the function in isolation. install_camilladsp() installs v1.yml/outputd-cutover.yml without calling it. The live enforcement of the 0 dB ceiling actually runs through jasper.sound.camilla_yaml.ensure_volume_limit_db (Python), so there is no live safety hole today - this is an orphaned guard, not a disabled one, but it gives false confidence that install.sh has a bash-side belt-and-suspenders check on shipped configs.
  - _Fix:_ Delete the function and its 3 tests, since the Python contract is the real 0 dB authority. (Wiring it into install_camilladsp as a pre-copy gate is also valid but heavier.)

### Duplication / SSOT — 235

- **[DA-0152]** `should-fix` · duplication · `AGENTS.md` :: Profile guardian — self-heal after filesystem loss
  - The Wi-Fi "Profile guardian" subsection (lines ~1412-1534, ~120 lines) substantially restates docs/HANDOFF-resilience.md's "WiFi profile recovery" section (lines 984-1150) instead of summarizing-and-linking, breaking this file's own single-source-of-truth rule.
  - _Evidence:_ Both sections independently narrate the same 2026-05-23 incident, the same guardian architecture (env file path/mode/keys), the same state-transition logic (steady_state/stash_stale/activate/recreate_attempt — pseudocode in AGENTS.md, prose bullets in the HANDOFF), the same 3-layer PSK-redaction description, and near-identical diagnostic commands. Contrast with the AEC-bridge section's "three layered bugs" and "NS=low+AGC1" passages, which compress to a few sentences and point to HANDOFF-aec.md for the full write-up — the pattern this section should follow.
  - _Fix:_ Trim the AGENTS.md subsection to a short operational summary (what it does, how to toggle/verify) and link to HANDOFF-resilience.md for the incident narrative, state machine, and PSK-redaction detail — mirror the AEC section's compress-and-link style.
- **[DA-0153]** `should-fix` · duplication · `c/jts-ring-ioplug/jts_ring_shm.c` :: jts_ring_writer_open / jts_ring_reader_open
  - The writer-open and reader-open create/attach/torn-reclaim paths are duplicated near-verbatim instead of sharing one helper.
  - _Evidence:_ init_created (168-202) vs init_created_reader (544-563): identical ftruncate/mmap/header-init/magic-publish, differing only in final struct fill. attach_existing (227-276) vs attach_existing_reader (568-610): identical fstat/mmap/wait_for_magic/geometry-cross-check chain. jts_ring_writer_open (278-359) vs jts_ring_reader_open (612-717): identical 8-attempt create/EEXIST/attach/torn-reclaim retry loop.
  - _Fix:_ Factor ftruncate+mmap+header-init+magic-publish, the fstat+mmap+wait_for_magic+geometry-check attach, and the 8-attempt retry/reclaim loop into shared static helpers filling common fields via out-params; leave only the distinct post-attach stamp per side (reader_fill_common already shows the pattern).
- **[DA-0154]** `should-fix` · duplication · `deploy/assets/bluetooth/bluetooth.css` :: .spinner / @keyframes bt-spin:208-227
  - bluetooth.css, dial.css, and home-assistant.css each hand-roll a near-identical rotating-spinner class + @keyframes, contradicting app.css's own stated layering rule ("Anything used by more than one page belongs here").
  - _Evidence:_ bluetooth.css:209-227 (.spinner/@keyframes bt-spin), dial.css:143-157 (.spinner/@keyframes dial-spin), home-assistant.css:116-138 (.ha-spinner/@keyframes ha-spin) are structurally identical (border+border-top-color+50% radius+0.8s linear infinite, plus a prefers-reduced-motion override). deploy/assets/wifi/wifi.css (outside this tile) has a fourth copy (@keyframes wifi-spin).
  - _Fix:_ Promote one .spinner into app.css parameterised by a --spinner-color var; delete the per-page copies (including wifi.css).
- **[DA-0155]** `should-fix` · duplication · `deploy/assets/correction/js/crossover/main.js` :: fetchJSON():44 / postWav():54
  - fetchJSON() and postWav() both end with an identical 5-line "parse JSON if possible, throw new Error(data.error || 'HTTP '+status) if !resp.ok" block; deploy/assets/correction/js/bass/main.js's load() inlines the same block a third time.
  - _Evidence:_ crossover/main.js:44-52 (fetchJSON) and :54-73 (postWav) share the identical tail; bass/main.js:63-79 (load()) repeats it verbatim. shared/js/http.js's private parseResponse() (used by postJSON) already implements the same data.error extraction, just not exported for GET use.
  - _Fix:_ Export a getJSON-with-error-extraction (or parseResponse) from shared/js/http.js and use it in all three sites.
- **[DA-0156]** `should-fix` · ssot · `deploy/assets/home-assistant/home-assistant.css` :: .row-version / .discover-list:15,44,50,57-58,66,70,84,100,146
  - References var(--text-muted, #666) and var(--space-2|3|4, ...rem) throughout, but neither --text-muted nor any --space-N custom property is ever defined in the codebase, so these declarations silently use their hardcoded fallback and never the design token.

Sibling deploy/assets/rooms/rooms.css uses the same var(--X,#hex) "belt-and-suspenders" shape but with the real --muted token name.

- **[DA-0157]** `should-fix` · ssot · `deploy/assets/sound-profile/sound.css` :: .toggle block, lines 836-852
  - sound.css redefines the canonical `.toggle` checkbox switch (48x28px, 28px track radius, 22px thumb, 0.18s transition) that AGENTS.md documents as living solely in app.css, and app.css already defines it differently (44x24px, 999px radius, 18px thumb, 150ms transition). Because canonical_page() links /assets/app.css before the page's page_css, this same-specificity rule in sound.css wins the cascade, so every `.toggle` on /sound/ (e.g. the match-loudness switch built at sound-profile/js/main.js:674) renders at a visibly different size than the toggle on every other canonical page (e.g. /rooms/'s wake-response and mains-highpass toggles, which correctly rely on app.css alone).
  - _Evidence:_ app.css line 540: `.toggle { position: relative; display: inline-block; width: 44px; height: 24px; flex: none; }`. sound.css line 837: `.toggle { position: relative; display: inline-block; flex-shrink: 0; width: 48px; height: 28px; }` (comment above it: "Canonical checkbox toggle (sage). Checkbox-based per web conventions." — suggesting the author believed this was the canonical home, unaware app.css already owns it). jasper/web/_common.py canonical_page(): app.css `<link>` at line 286, page_css/page_css_href in `head_extra` at line 287 (after). rooms.css, by contrast, has no `.toggle` rule and its own comment explicitly defers to app.css.
  - _Fix:_ Delete the .toggle / .toggle input / .toggle .track(::before) / :checked / reduced-motion block (~lines 836-852) from sound.css and rely on app.css, matching rooms.css.
- **[DA-0158]** `should-fix` · duplication · `deploy/assets/tools/js/main.js` :: load/onToggle/onApply
  - ~90 lines (toolsOf/packsOf/load/onToggle/onApply) are duplicated near-verbatim between main.js and detail.js, and the duplication has already visibly drifted in user-facing copy.
  - _Evidence:_ main.js uses typographic punctuation in status text ("Enabling "+key+"…" line 121, " — Apply to restart" line 129, "about 10–15 seconds…" line 162); detail.js's copy-pasted equivalents use plain ASCII ("..." line 109/213/229, " - Apply to restart" line 117). main.js's own onCardClick/onCardKeydown/onApply/onToggle have zero dedicated test, unlike detail.js's twin (tools_detail_harness.mjs).
  - _Fix:_ Extract the truly-identical onToggle/onApply (and their copy strings) into a shared tools/js helper parameterized by base path, imported by both entry points; load()/render() differ more so leave those or share incrementally.

  - Duplicates ~40 lines of deploy/bin/jasper-camilla-pipe-guard's repair_statefile() (:99-129) and the FIFO reader-presence probe from check_playback_pipe_or_repair() (:131-154) inline, instead of sharing a lib. The codebase already hit this exact failure mode once (deploy/lib/jasper-core-graph-park-units.sh's header: a list 'duplicated byte-for-byte...with no shared source and no test pinning them equal...a future edit to one...would drift the other') and fixed it with a shared lib + tests/test_core_graph_park_units_contract.py. No analogous lib or test exists for this pair.
  - _Fix:_ Extract repair_statefile() + the reader-presence probe into deploy/lib/jasper-camilla-guard-common.sh, sourced sibling-first/installed-fallback (like jasper-env-file.sh), parameterized on the detail= message; add a small contract test pinning the two guards' shared logic, mirroring test_core_graph_park_units_contract.py.

  - _Evidence:_ Lines 2219-2291, e.g. `trim_db: float | None = None\nif "trim_db" in body:\n    try:\n        trim_db = float(body["trim_db"])\n    except (TypeError, ValueError):\n        self._send_json({"error": "trim_db must be a number"}, status=400)\n        return` repeated with only the key/caster/message swapped for client_latency_ms (int), left_delay_ms, right_delay_ms, crossover_hz (float), then the same pattern again for the two bool fields via isinstance.
  - _Fix:_ Extract a numeric _parse_optional(body,key,caster,type_name) that sends the 400 itself for the 5 numeric fields, plus a small _parse_optional_bool for the 2 bool fields (they use isinstance, not try/except, so one helper won't cover all seven uniformly).

Near-duplicate variants (same mono/DAC8x/woofer@0/tweeter@1 shape) also live in test_active_speaker_staging.py:33, test_active_speaker_setup_status.py:29, test_active_speaker_readiness.py:101, test_active_speaker_topology_tone.py:23, test_active_speaker_measurement.py:21. tests/conftest.py is only 65 lines, one autouse env-isolation fixture -- no shared topology builder exists. staging.py's copy already diverges by parametrizing `protection_status` instead of hardcoding it, showing the copies are drifting apart.
  - _Fix:_ Extract one mono_2way_topology() builder (kwargs for identity_verified/protection_status) into tests/conftest.py and import it in the 7 files.
- **[DA-0235]** `should-fix` · duplication · `tests/test_build_wake_negative_feature_bank.py` :: FakeExtractor / _write_wav / _write_bundle
  - Test fixture scaffolding is duplicated near byte-for-byte with tests/test_build_wake_feature_bank.py (a third near-copy also exists in tests/test_wake_training_feature_bank.py, outside this tile).
  - _Evidence:_ diff of lines 1-70 of both files: only the module-name strings differ ('build_wake_feature_bank' vs 'build_wake_negative_feature_bank'); the FakeExtractor class, _write_wav(), and _write_bundle() bodies are identical.

- **[DA-0237]** `should-fix` · ssot · `tests/test_install_core_audio_graph_loop.py` :: EXPECTED_DSTS
  - The hand-maintained EXPECTED_DSTS tuple (asserted to be 'every destination the install table should attempt') has drifted from the real JASPER_CORE_AUDIO_GRAPH_INSTALL_ROWS array it mirrors, silently narrowing this deploy-safety test's coverage.
  - _Evidence:_ EXPECTED_DSTS lists 15 destinations; deploy/lib/install/systemd-units.sh's JASPER_CORE_AUDIO_GRAPH_INSTALL_ROWS (lines 94-112) has 17, missing 'jasper-xvf-firmware-update.service' and 'jasper-fanin-pitch-neutralize' from the test. Tests only assert `dst in attempted` per EXPECTED_DSTS item (one-directional), so a regression dropping either of those 2 real rows from the transactional install loop -- exactly the 'silently skip a later unit' deploy hazard this file exists to catch -- would not fail.
  - _Fix:_ Add the two missing destinations to EXPECTED_DSTS (all 17) and change the loops to assert `attempted == set(EXPECTED_DSTS)` so any future drop fails loudly; parsing the array from the fragment at test time is the fuller SSOT fix but not required.
- **[DA-0238]** `should-fix` · duplication · `tests/test_voice_daemon_defects.py` :: :19-34 (httpx/sounddevice/rapidfuzz sys.modules stub)
  - 5 files (this one, test_voice_daemon_end_turn_reentry.py, test_voice_daemon_manual_start_guard.py, test_voice_daemon_mute_click.py, test_voice_daemon_teardown_end_segment.py) install a fake httpx into sys.modules via `if "httpx" not in sys.modules: sys.modules["httpx"] = <fake>` — a check that can't distinguish 'genuinely not installed' from 'not yet imported by anything'. httpx is a real, always-declared project dependency (pyproject.toml) consumed with real APIs (Client/MockTransport/Response) by test_voice_model_discovery.py and test_voice_setup.py in this same tile.
  - _Evidence:_ Reproduced the exact guard in an isolated Python process: once the fake is installed, a later plain `import httpx` (as those two files do) silently binds to the cached fake and `httpx.Client` raises AttributeError. The sibling file test_voice_daemon_mute_privacy.py already has a safer `_stub_if_missing` helper (tries `__import__(name)` first) with a comment: 'a fake httpx shadowing a real install breaks jasper.tools imports' — proving the team hit exactly this failure mode once and fixed it in only one of six files. Currently masked only because 7 alphabetically-earlier files (test_bus.py etc.) import real httpx first.
  - _Fix:_ Hoist the existing `_stub_if_missing` helper into tests/conftest.py (or at minimum replace the 5 naive guards with it) so the fake is only installed when httpx is genuinely absent.
- **[DA-0239]** `should-fix` · duplication · `tests/test_wake_corpus_setup.py` :: _serve_in_thread helper, 23 call sites e.g. test_level_sse_returns_event_stream_headers:1451 through test_api_session_enable_bridge_outputs_then_begins:4153
  - ~22 test bodies each hand-roll the identical live-HTTP-server try/finally teardown instead of a fixture, despite the exact fixture idiom already established by sibling files in the same tests/ directory.
  - _Evidence:_ grep shows `server, th, port = _serve_in_thread(backend)` at 23 sites, each followed by its own `finally: server.shutdown(); server.server_close(); th.join(timeout=2)` (~5 lines x22 ≈110 lines of pure repetition). Contrast tests/test_web_weather_setup.py:190-215 `live_server` fixture and tests/test_wake_setup.py:550 `running_server` fixture, which do this once and yield; this file's own `_mutating_status` helper (line 1527, reused by 4 tests) proves the author knows the pattern but didn't apply it broadly.
  - _Fix:_ Convert _serve_in_thread into a pytest fixture that starts the server, yields (port + helper), and tears down once; migrate the ~22 sites to consume it, mirroring live_server/running_server.
- **[DA-0240]** `should-fix` · duplication · `tests/test_web_airplay_setup.py` :: _FakeHandler
  - A ~39-line hand-rolled BaseHTTPRequestHandler fake is duplicated near byte-for-byte across at least 5 web-wizard test files, with no shared helper despite one already existing for a sibling concern in this exact suite.

### Test hygiene — 61

- **[DA-0241]** `should-fix` · untested · `jasper/route_latency/mic_readers.py` :: build_mic_reader
  - The operator-facing `--mic` spec parser (bare/`udp`/`udp:<port>`/`alsa:<device>`/unrecognized branches) and `AlsaMicReader` have no direct unit test — only reachable in the test suite by monkeypatching `build_mic_reader` away entirely.
  - _Evidence:_ `grep -rn 'build_mic_reader(' tests/` shows only `monkeypatch.setattr(harness, "build_mic_reader", lambda spec: reader)` call sites in test_route_latency_harness.py; no test calls `build_mic_reader(spec)` itself with any of the 5 spec forms, so port-parsing (`int(spec.split(':',1)[1])`), the alsa: empty-device ValueError, and the unrecognized-spec ValueError are all unverified.
  - _Fix:_ Add direct tests: build_mic_reader('') and ('udp:9999') return UdpMicReader on the right port; ('alsa:hw:1,0') builds AlsaMicReader with alsaaudio mocked; ('alsa:') and ('bogus') raise ValueError.

The 'dial_heartbeat' hits in tests/test_control_server.py test a different thing (jasper.control.server's own `_dial_heartbeat`/`_load_dial_heartbeat` state persistence), not this check's interpretation of `control.get_dial_status()`'s ok/warn/unreachable branches.

- **[DA-0260]** `should-fix` · untested · `rust/jasper-resampler/src/lib.rs` :: AudioRing::push_interleaved :335-349
  - The ring's drop-oldest-on-overflow branch (`if self.fill_frames() == self.capacity_frames { self.read_frame += 1; dropped += 1; }`) and its `dropped: u64` return value — the one piece of behavior that makes this a genuine ring rather than a plain buffer — are never exercised by any test in the crate's ~30-test suite.
  - _Evidence:_ Every test calling push_interleaved sizes the ring comfortably larger than what's pushed: trim_to_keeps_newest_frames_down_to_target (capacity 4096, pushes 1000), trim_to_is_noop_when_at_or_below_target (capacity 1024, pushes 100), trim_to_leaves_a_usable_window_for_the_cursor (capacity 8192, pushes 4096); resample_i16's internal capacity is sized to `frames + TAPS + 1` so it never overflows by construction. No test asserts push_interleaved's return value is nonzero. This is the concrete, real piece of the Phase-0 hint's 'low test density' concern — the rest of the suite is actually strong.
  - _Fix:_ Add a test pushing more frames than capacity_frames, asserting the returned drop count equals the overrun and that the newest capacity_frames survive while dropped frames read 0.

- **[DA-0262]** `should-fix` · low-quality · `tests/test_laptop_onboarding_scripts.py` :: repo_env_local
  - repo_env_local() mutates the real repo-root .env.local file (not tmp_path) and is used by 8 test methods in this class, with no synchronization, while the project's own documented merge lane runs pytest in parallel.
  - _Evidence:_ repo_env_local() (lines 82-97) does `ENV_LOCAL.write_text(...)` / `ENV_LOCAL.unlink()` directly on `ROOT / ".env.local"`, restoring the prior bytes only in a `finally`. scripts/test-merge runs `exec "${pytest_bin}" ... -n 4 "$@"` (pytest-xdist, default `--dist load`, which schedules individual test items to workers independently -- confirmed no `--dist loadscope/loadfile` or `xdist_group` marker exists anywhere in the repo). AGENTS.md's 'Agent test routing' section documents this merge lane explicitly as 'the full hardware-free pytest lane: parallel pytest'. The same file (15 lines below, test_write_laptop_state_persists_ip_and_speaker_separately) already shows the safe alternative: overriding REPO_ROOT to point at a tmp dir.
  - _Fix:_ Serialize the class with @pytest.mark.xdist_group(name="env_local") so xdist keeps its items on one worker (smallest, test-only fix that kills the parallel race). Fuller fix: add a REPO_ROOT override seam in _lib.sh (REPO_ROOT="${REPO_ROOT:-...}") so run_deploy can target tmp_path and never touches the real .env.local.
