## Completeness critic (verbatim)

# Completeness Critic — auditing the JTS Deep Audit (SHA 9a24d453)

## Bottom line up front

The audit's mechanics are sound and its coverage arithmetic reconciles exactly (1506 tiled source + 18 binary-skipped + 129 docs-deferred = 1653 tracked). The per-file comb was **real, not rubber-stamped** — my 3 random spot-reads each had a legitimate Phase-1 finding I independently confirm. But the audit has **two structural blind spots that let at least two real, same-day-fixed bugs through**, and it audited a **branch that is not `main` and is already 14 commits / 206 files stale.** The honest coverage claim needs three asterisks, below.

---

## (a) VERIFIED-MISSING — concrete gaps with evidence

### 1. `[next-round work]` MISSED BUG — silent HTTP-200 on failed source-toggle persist (honesty violation)
- **File the audit read:** `jasper/web/sources_setup.py` (tile T058).
- **Evidence at the audited SHA** (`git show 9a24d453:jasper/web/sources_setup.py`, lines 242–290): `_set_unit`/`_manage_unit` call the restart broker and, on `not resp.get("ok")`, **only `logger.warning(...)` — they never raise.** The handler returns 200 regardless. The docstring rationalizes it: *"Failures are logged but not raised — partial state ... is rare and self-heals on the next toggle."* Under the WS1 Phase-3b non-root privilege drop, `manage-unit-files` is polkit-denied, so **every** toggle's persistence failed with "Interactive authentication required" while returning 200 — "a toggle that lied."
- **The audit's verdict on this exact file:** *"Reachable (/sources/, port 8773), **thoroughly tested toggle page**; duplicates `_systemctl` and `_send_json` helpers"* — i.e. only duplication nits. It looked straight at `_set_unit` (flagged its `_systemctl` twin) and **accepted the file's own "self-heals" comment** instead of challenging it (playbook rule 1: comments are evidence to verify, not obey).
- **Confirmation it was real:** maintainers found and fixed it independently in **origin/main #1206** (`2c0c33a8`, landed hours after the audit's fork), adding a root helper `jasper/source_intent.py` and `test_rule_does_not_grant_manage_unit_files`.
- **Why static reading missed it:** the failure lives in the seam **non-root web → restart broker → polkit rules**, which sit in *different tiles* (T058 vs the broker/polkit tiles). No single reader saw the authority path, and there was no cross-cutting privilege lens. This is also a **"wrong-question" instance** the task named: a security/authority-sensitive file judged against a duplication/style rubric.

### 2. `[next-round work]` MISSED BUG — Rust build-cache mtime trap ships stale daemon binaries
- **File the audit read:** `.../deploy/lib/install/rust-daemons.sh` (270 LOC, tile T094).
- **Evidence:** mtime-preserving `rsync -a` staging + cargo's mtime-based freshness → a changed source can land "in the past," cargo declares `Fresh`, and `install.sh` reinstalls the **stale** binary while reporting success. **Proven live on jts.local 2026-07-10** (audit day) and explicitly "same class as the 2026-07-02 stale `jasper-usbsink-audio` incident" — a *recurring* deploy-integrity (blocker-taxonomy: deploy/rollback) bug.
- **The audit's engagement:** `rust-daemons.sh` appears in the Phase-1 output only *incidentally* (cross-referenced from T123's host-clock `Cargo.toml` reachability note). No finding on the mtime trap. Phase-2 "mtime" hits are about an unrelated test fixture.
- **Confirmation it was real:** fixed in **origin/main #1208** (`e3f62ea3`) with `tests/test_rust_build_cache_staging.py`.
- **Why missed:** requires reasoning across the `rsync -a` mtime → cargo-freshness → compile boundary, and the audit **executed nothing** (no build, no hardware). No standalone deploy/resilience lens existed to hunt this class.

### 3. `[accepted-gap candidate]` usbsink Python bridge / lean-FIFO — under-escalated, then deleted on main
- The audit **correctly** graded `jasper/usbsink/audio_bridge.py`/`daemon.py` "mixed, **lab-only**, opt-in via `JASPER_USBSINK_PYTHON_LAB_ALLOW=1`" and correctly graded the *Rust* `jasper-usbsink-audio` as the earns-its-keep ExecStart target. (I initially suspected a reachability misattribution; on verification the audit got this right — noting it for honesty.)
- The soft gap: `docs/HANDOFF-usb-low-latency.md:1650` carried an explicit **"Delete after Rust bridge covers hotplug/state"** condition — a satisfied "remove-after-X" the debt sweep (acknowledged: 3/403 checked, no git-blame) never adjudicated. The audit kept it at nit ("fix a stale comment"); **main #1200 deleted the whole subsystem** (6 prod `.py` + 2 `.rs` + 10 tests). Defensible judgment call, not a hard miss → accepted-gap.

### 4. `[next-round work]` Subsystem-splitting tile boundaries (the mechanism behind #1 and #2)
Verified splits where no single reader owned the cross-file behavior:
- **Rust `jasper-fanin` crate split across 6 tiles** (T005 mixer / T012 lane_resampler / T025 config / T027 state / T032 host_compliance / T082 fifo+host_clock+impulse_tap). Intra-crate data flow (config→state→mixer) had no single owner.
- **C-ring SPSC contract split:** producer `c/jts-ring-ioplug` (T068) vs Rust consumers `jasper-fanin/src/fifo.rs` (T082) and `jasper-outputd/src/shm_ring_source.rs` (T088). The single-producer/single-consumer ring invariant crosses three tiles.
- **Volume subsystem split:** `volume_coordinator.py` alone in T029, `volume_observers/persistence/curve/diagnostics` in T092. The coordinator-vs-measurement race that **main #1213** just fixed lives exactly across this seam ("during measure" = 0 hits in the audit output despite 206 "reconcil"/122 "measurement" hits).

---

## (b) Reader-quality calibration verdict — GOOD, with a systematic (not per-file) weakness

I pulled 3 pseudo-random production files (seed 20260711) and read them hard against Phase 1:

| File | My read | Phase-1 finding | Verdict |
|---|---|---|---|
| `jasper/route_latency/mic_readers.py` | High quality; loud-failure discipline, frozen wire constants cross-checked by test | Flagged `build_mic_reader`/`AlsaMicReader` as **untested** (only reachable via monkeypatch) | Confirmed, fair |
| `jasper/cli/wake_enroll.py` | `record_window`+`quadrant_dirs` are test-only backward-compat shims (run_session uses `record_legs`/`all_quadrant_dirs`) | Flagged both as **dead production code** | Confirmed independently |
| `jasper/sound/runtime.py` | — | Flagged `stage_lean_capture_config` + `LEAN_STAGED_CONFIG_NAME` as **dead** | Correct — and main #1200/#1209 then deleted the lean pipeline |

**Calibration:** 3/3 random files carried a real Phase-1 finding I agree with. The comb was genuine. The weakness is **not per-file laziness** — it's structural: both confirmed misses (#1, #2) are cross-subsystem *runtime/authority/deploy* behaviors invisible to reading any one file in isolation. The reader that missed #1 was the same reader that correctly found dead code two functions away; it just accepted the file's self-exculpating comment about the swallowed failure.

---

## (c) Load-bearing claims still unverified by any phase

Checked ~8 invariants from AGENTS.md/README against all three phase outputs:

- **VERIFIED:** CamillaDSP safety ceiling / 0 dB clamp (AGENTS:1025-1028) — pinned by `tests/test_audio_safety_pins.py::test_every_static_camilladsp_config_caps_volume_at_zero_db`, and Phase 1 read it. Reconciler single-writers — `JASPER_MIC_DEVICE_*` and `jasper-aec-reconcile` explicitly verified ("Single writer of…; matches AGENTS.md pattern-3 doctrine").
- **UNVERIFIED — `jasper-outputd` is "the only normal writer to the physical DAC"** (README:133): **zero** occurrences of "only normal writer" in any phase output; no dedicated guard test surfaced. A central hardware-safety single-writer claim nobody adjudicated.
- **UNVERIFIED — multiroom peering "picks exactly one winner per wake event"** (README:606): **zero** "exactly one winner" occurrences in any phase; the grouping/peering tests found are surface/registry tests, not a winner-election guard.
- **Global caveat on every "pinned by test X" claim:** the audit **executed no tests** (static-only, acknowledged). So each "tested?" verdict means *a reader saw the test source*, not *the test passes on this tree*. #1's file was called "thoroughly tested" precisely because its tests **mock the broker to succeed**, so they never exercised the real non-root/polkit denial — a happy-path-only pin that a green-run would not have caught either, but which reading the tests adversarially might have.

---

## (d) Drift-since-SHA status — the audited tree is a stale, divergent branch

- **Branch itself: static.** `git log 9a24d453..HEAD` = 0 commits. The audit is current w.r.t. its own branch.
- **But it is NOT `main` and not an ancestor of `main`.** Merge-base with `origin/main` = `b584df3e` (2026-07-10 15:57). The audited SHA = merge-base **+1 commit** ("audio: isolate optional AEC reference from playback", not on main). `origin/main` tip (2026-07-11 05:12) = merge-base **+14 commits**.
- **Drift surface:** `git diff b584df3e origin/main` = **206 files, +16,177 / −13,862**, including **18 files the audit read, now deleted** on main (6 prod `.py`: `usbsink_main`, `usbsink/{audio_bridge,daemon,output_mode_reconcile,preempt_listener,state_publisher}`; 2 `.rs`; 10 usbsink/lean tests) via #1200/#1209.
- **Of the 14 main commits, ~6-7 are fixes for bugs that pre-existed the audited SHA** (#1206 sources honesty, #1208 stale binaries, #1213 volume-reconcile-during-measurement, #1211 shairport reviving a disabled unit, #1210 crossover ports, #1203 install SSOT). I **confirmed 2 (#1206, #1208)** were in files the audit opened and missed; the others are strong candidates I did not fully adjudicate.

**Net:** the audit's findings describe a tree that no longer exists as-is; part of its usbsink coverage is mooted, and `main` independently caught bugs the audit didn't.

Minor drift-adjacent nit: `tests/test_capture_relay_crypto.py:115` still skips with *"capture page not present on this branch (lands with step 3)"*, but `capture-page/js/crypto.js` and `tests/js/capture_crypto_emit.mjs` both exist at the SHA — stale skip message (the cross-language crypto proof does run when `node` is present).

---

## (e) Honest assessment — is "100% of files opened, findings adversarially verified" TRUE?

**Literally true, with three asterisks.** The 1506/1506 tiling reconciles exactly against `git ls-files` (1506 + 18 binary + 129 docs = 1653), and the 69/667 rejection rate is real evidence the adversarial verifier bit down rather than flattered. But: **(\*1) it is 100% of a divergent branch that is not `main`, already 14 commits / 206 files / 18-deletions stale** — the coverage claim should read "100% of the audited fork," not "of the codebase." **(\*2) "opened" ≠ "understood in context":** at least two real, same-day-fixed bugs (silent-200 toggle honesty #1206; stale-binary deploy trap #1208) lived in files that were opened and passed, because each failure spans a tile boundary — non-root→broker→polkit, and cargo-mtime→`rsync -a`→freshness — that no tile owned and no cross-cutting **privilege / resilience / deploy** lens swept (those lenses were deliberately de-scoped into the per-file rubric, which by construction cannot see cross-file runtime interactions). **(\*3) static-only:** nothing was executed, so deploy/runtime/authority correctness is structurally out of reach, and every "pinned by test X" means "a reader read the test," not "it passed here." The strongest single piece of evidence for the critic: the #1206 bug was **rationalised past, not overlooked** — the reader saw the swallowed failure and the code's own "self-heals on the next toggle" comment, and believed the comment. That is the failure mode the playbook names first, and it is the one to instrument for next round (a privilege/authority + deploy-integrity lens, and re-basing the audit onto `main`).
